  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText10239144217582718285" style="display:none">Deep in the African rain forest, near the legendary ruins of the Lost City of Zinj, an expedition of eight American geologists is mysteriously and brutally killed in a matter of minutes.<br /><br />Ten thousand miles away, Karen Ross, the Congo Project Supervisor, watches a gruesome video transmission of the aftermath: a camp destroyed, tents crushed and torn, equipment scattered in the mud alongside dead bodies — all motionless except for one moving image — a grainy, dark, man-shaped blur.<br /><br />In San Francisco, primatologist Peter Elliot works with Amy, a gorilla with an extraordinary vocabulary of 620 “signs,” the most ever learned by a primate, and she likes to fingerpaint. But recently, her behavior has been erratic and her drawings match, with stunning accuracy, the brittle pages of a Portuguese print dating back to 1642 . . . a drawing of an ancient lost city. A new expedition — along with Amy — is sent into the Congo where they enter a secret world, and the only way out may be through a horrifying death …<br />source: michaelcrichton.com</span>

I am just a sensitive soul. I can take some animal death. I just didn&#39;t want to read this, if it was some sort of blood-bath, lol. I could care less if the people die, i am just worried about the animals and/or apes, lol. Thank you!</a>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Wow, it's been 44 days since you asked this but no one answered yet so here you go. There are a few animal deaths but they are not without reason (sel<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Wow, it's been 44 days since you asked this but no one answered yet so here you go. There are a few animal deaths but they are not without reason (self defense without ruining too much) and there's definitely a lot more people who die than animals. The book definitely does not condone animal cruelty. If you are an animal person, you probably will like the story about Amy the ape. She's based on an ape in real life (I think her name is koko). <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_285969330" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/285969330" />
    <a title="mark monday" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday"><img alt="mark monday" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572672245p2/131922.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/285969330?book_show_action=true">Feb 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="mark monday" class="user" itemprop="url" name="mark monday" href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday">mark monday</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780061782558" href="/book/show/6326950-congo">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131922-mark-monday?shelf=blood-and-danger">blood-and-danger</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer285969330" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6998589698210230911">i'm having a little trouble with myself right now. i just gave this one 4 stars and Inner-Snob Mark is getting very twitchy, almost trigger-happy, ready to take control of my favorite hand and bump this one down to 3 stars. never fear, i have a tight rein on Inner-Snob Mark and have carefully compartmentalized him away tonight. but he does have a few good points. my God, i gave the timeless classic The Last Unicorn 3 stars. i gave Room - which wrecked me emotionally and had me crying like someon</span>
  <span id="freeText6998589698210230911" style="display:none">i'm having a little trouble with myself right now. i just gave this one 4 stars and Inner-Snob Mark is getting very twitchy, almost trigger-happy, ready to take control of my favorite hand and bump this one down to 3 stars. never fear, i have a tight rein on Inner-Snob Mark and have carefully compartmentalized him away tonight. but he does have a few good points. my God, i gave the timeless classic The Last Unicorn 3 stars. i gave Room - which wrecked me emotionally and had me crying like someone died - the same 4 stars. and Congo gets only 1 star less than either Picnic at Hanging Rock or The Thin Red Line - two books that i think are perfect from beginning to end. eh, so fucken what. stars are stupid, right?<br /><br />okay, so that's the disclaimer. it will probably be longer than the actual review.<br /><br />i LOVED this book. it was one of those immersive experiences, one that i dived into and stayed deep. Crichton is not known for having an interesting writing style, but his prose is clean &amp; straightforward &amp; dry without being off-puttingly clinical. <i>ack, Inner-Snob Mark just had a spasm when i used the words "Crichton" and "prose" in the same sentence.</i> no complaints whatsoever about the quality of writing. Congo is not corny and it is not emotionally manipulative and there aren't stupid lines where i start breathing loudly in frustration. what it does have is a superbly brisk narrative that does not falter despite the very dense level of information surrounding it. and that's another great thing: the very well-done infodumps. i'm going to sound a little schoolboy-ish here... but i learned so much! about the Congo, of course. but this being Crichton, i also learned a lot about apes and technology and corporate philosophies and tons of other interesting shite. the author makes sure all of his research is on the page and yet it didn't feel didactic and it didn't take away from the plot - if anything, it drew me in further.<br /><br />oh yeah, and it had one more awesome thing. in my GR friend Bill's words: <i>The big star in this story is Amy, a gorilla with a 620 sign vocabulary. After reading this, you will want a gorilla for a best friend.</i> ah, Amy... i know we would be fast friends!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6998589698210230911" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_399561065" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/399561065" />
    <a title="Michael Fierce" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6880123-michael-fierce"><img alt="Michael Fierce" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602282713p2/6880123.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/399561065?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Fierce" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Fierce" href="/user/show/6880123-michael-fierce">Michael Fierce</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/10419175-congo">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of cryptid adventures and for those who love giant apes &amp; gorillas</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6880123-michael-fierce?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6880123-michael-fierce?shelf=creature">creature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6880123-michael-fierce?shelf=apes">apes</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer399561065" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15970227368116009436"><pre>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380388886i/749719.jpg' width='260' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  <br/>
</pre><br/>First off, I've always gone bananas over books and movies that have giant apes & big gorillas in them, going way back to when I was a kid, particularly with movie classics like, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13578816.King_Kong' title='King Kong by Delos W. Lovelace' rel='nofollow noopener'>King Kong</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12638044.Mighty_Joe_Young' title='Mighty Joe Young by Ernest B. Schoedsack' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mighty Joe Young</a>, that were a blast for me and my brother to watch together.<br/><br/>Reading books and watching movies about big apes helps me reconnect with those experiences I will always hold dear to me.<br/><br/>I've been going ape over everything & anything simian fiction-related ever since. <br/><br/>When I first saw the p</span>
  <span id="freeText15970227368116009436" style="display:none"><pre>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380388886i/749719.jpg" width="260" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
</pre><br>First off, I've always gone bananas over books and movies that have giant apes &amp; big gorillas in them, going way back to when I was a kid, particularly with movie classics like, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13578816.King_Kong" title="King Kong by Delos W. Lovelace" rel="nofollow noopener">King Kong</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12638044.Mighty_Joe_Young" title="Mighty Joe Young by Ernest B. Schoedsack" rel="nofollow noopener">Mighty Joe Young</a>, that were a blast for me and my brother to watch together.<br><br>Reading books and watching movies about big apes helps me reconnect with those experiences I will always hold dear to me.<br><br>I've been going ape over everything &amp; anything simian fiction-related ever since. <br><br>When I first saw the preview for the movie, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1014377.Congo" title="Congo by Michael Crichton" rel="nofollow noopener">Congo</a>, it was a no-brainer that I would be seeing it as soon as it came out. <br><br>Anyone who may have seen the original advertisements for the movie may remember that the 1st preview centered on character, <b>Charles Travis</b>, played by fan-favorite actor, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1362939.Bruce_Campbell" title="Bruce Campbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Bruce Campbell</a>. <b>*</b>Ever since I first saw <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6072791.Evil_Dead_Companion" title="Evil Dead Companion by Bill Warren" rel="nofollow noopener">Evil Dead</a>, starring <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1362939.Bruce_Campbell" title="Bruce Campbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Bruce Campbell</a> as <b>Ash</b>, I followed every single film he did. But, if you saw <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1323174.Making_of_Congo" title="Making of Congo by Jody Duncan" rel="nofollow noopener">Congo</a>, then you'll know that he was only in the film for about 5 minutes or less! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1407892167i/10776131._SX540_.jpg" width="384" height="226" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I rushed out to see the 1st showing on the 1st day of the film release with my best friend, Doug, at the time. <br><br><b>Before I read the book</b>. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380388886i/749721._SX540_.jpg" width="384" height="216" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I knew it was gonna have a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7653482.Jurassic_Park" title="Jurassic Park by Michael Crichton" rel="nofollow noopener">Jurassic Park</a> sorta cheeziness to it but I was looking forward to that and otherwise not really knowing what else to expect. The acting was a mixed bag of fine performances like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/571279.Laura_Linney" title="Laura Linney" rel="nofollow noopener">Laura Linney</a> and <b>Dylan Walsh</b>, along with some of the worst acting since the very dawn of time. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/258912.Tim_Curry" title="Tim Curry" rel="nofollow noopener">Tim Curry</a>, an actor I've loved since watching his iconic legendary performance as <b>Dr. Frank-N-Furter</b> in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3199596.The_Official_Rocky_Horror_Picture_Show_Movie_Novel" title="The Official Rocky Horror Picture Show Movie Novel by Richard J. Anobile" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rocky Horror Picture Show</a> many many times, was just God-awful! As <b>Herkermer Homolka</b>, his Russian accent defies logic as to why they would even keep the cameras rolling after his first line, Which, to me, sounded like he got his tongue stuck in his throat. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380388886i/749722._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="280" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Though, by this point, I wouldn't trade him in for the world though his is the worst accent I've ever heard! <b>*</b>Now that I think about it, the way over-the-top French accent by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3867723.Julia_Ormond" title="Julia Ormond" rel="nofollow noopener">Julia Ormond</a> in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8456710.Mad_Men_the_Illustrated_World" title="Mad Men the Illustrated World by Dyna Moe" rel="nofollow noopener">Mad Men</a> is definitely up there for debate! ~ I'm guessing that the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8456710.Mad_Men_the_Illustrated_World" title="Mad Men the Illustrated World by Dyna Moe" rel="nofollow noopener">Mad Men</a> producers must've got confused thinking she was French actress, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/730909.Juliette_Binoche" title="Juliette Binoche" rel="nofollow noopener">Juliette Binoche</a>, when they brought her on, since they look dead-on identical!:<br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://0d.img.v4.skyrock.net/2749/19572749/pics/2999350835_1_3_NMfXs8Cv.jpg">http://0d.img.v4.skyrock.net/2749/195...</a><br><br>Back to Congo. As my buddy Doug and I watched the film we kept sinking lower and lower and lower into our seats until we were, seriously, nearly sitting on the floor. Throughout all the impossibilities that could <i>only</i> happen in an 80's movie, we burst out laughing in places where we weren't supposed to dozens of times! (much to the hatred of the rest of the audience, I'm sure). By the end of the movie, as we were walking out, I said in my best Amy voice - the pet gorilla who had the female equivalent of a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1401.Stephen_Hawking" title="Stephen Hawking" rel="nofollow noopener">Stephen Hawking</a>-like computer voicebox -<b>
  <i> "Bad movie, Amy, Bad movie."</i>
</b> Yeah...we were little shi†s then just like most guys that age, I guess.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380388886i/749723.png" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Just so you know, I've watched the film a few times since and it gets better every time. It's a real hoot! and now I think I love it!<br><br>But, back to the book. <br><br>In case it surprises anybody, I don't think <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5194.Michael_Crichton" title="Michael Crichton" rel="nofollow noopener">Michael Crichton</a> wrote this one <b>just so</b> it would turn out to be a mega-million-buck movie. <br><br>And though it's a tech-thriller, it's also a throwback to the pulp adventure-style books going on for over a century now. Most notably, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/751789.King_Solomon_s_Mines" title="King Solomon's Mines by H. Rider Haggard" rel="nofollow noopener">King Solomon's Mines</a>:<br><pre>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380388886i/749724.jpg" width="297" height="460" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</pre><br>The difference? It's been updated, everything moves faster, there's better equipment, and <i>everybody's</i> more sarcastic and cynical than ever before. No duh. Really!?<br><br>I enjoyed this novel. I'm pretty sure everybody has an idea what it's about so why go into it. <br><br>It was a good book. <br><br>However...<br><br>Since most of the covers, including the movie poster and dvd, have a GORILLA on it, you would expect there to be some damn gorillas IN IT. <br><br>I kept asking:<br><pre>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1407546511i/10737496.jpg" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</pre><br>...a common question I ask whenever I expect to see more of something, or, when there's an element sorely missing throughout what I'm reading!<br><br>Here's one where you would want <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5194.Michael_Crichton" title="Michael Crichton" rel="nofollow noopener">Michael Crichton</a> to use his time machine from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13573415.Timeline" title="Timeline by Michael Crichton" rel="nofollow noopener">Timeline</a> so he could fast forward to the future and take notes of the formula that worked so well in books he wrote later and were more successful. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7653482.Jurassic_Park" title="Jurassic Park by Michael Crichton" rel="nofollow noopener">Jurassic Park</a> had a great abundance of dinosaurs in it. Too bad he couldn't have used that same formula here!<br><br>It is a well written, nicely plotted book, with good characters, a great premise, action-packed, and mostly a lot of fun. <br><br>It was just missing one thing for me: <b>MORE FREAKING GORILLAS!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380388886i/749727._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="229" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>*</b> This is one of those rare books that has many great artwork covered editions. I hope you pick a good one. Buying the bland books allows the publisher to think it's ok to skip the art department, leaving us with a world of mediocre book covers to choose from. So you know, many of the cheapest editions have some very nice covers.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380388886i/749728.jpg" width="400" height="280" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="15970227368116009436" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2359242076" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Rohit Enghakat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15355957-rohit-enghakat"><img alt="Rohit Enghakat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588900052p2/15355957.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2359242076?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rohit Enghakat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rohit Enghakat" href="/user/show/15355957-rohit-enghakat">Rohit Enghakat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15355957-rohit-enghakat?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15355957-rohit-enghakat?shelf=techno-thriller">techno-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2359242076" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14376399476737614648">The book was interesting in the second half with the first half using lot of technical jargon which almost made me abandon it halfway. Once you overcome the first half, it becomes interesting and edgy. The author has described the African jungles so vividly that you visualise it right before your eyes. All about an organisation's quest to explore blue diamonds which sends a woman, Karen Ross accompanied by a primatologist, Peter Elliot who becomes the central character along with his pet gorilla</span>
  <span id="freeText14376399476737614648" style="display:none">The book was interesting in the second half with the first half using lot of technical jargon which almost made me abandon it halfway. Once you overcome the first half, it becomes interesting and edgy. The author has described the African jungles so vividly that you visualise it right before your eyes. All about an organisation's quest to explore blue diamonds which sends a woman, Karen Ross accompanied by a primatologist, Peter Elliot who becomes the central character along with his pet gorilla, Amy. You feel for Amy when she converses with her handler Peter Elliot. The expedition is led by a mercenary turned expert jungle guide Munro. There are the unusual twists and turns given the jungle backdrop, the tribals and the gorillas. The whole technical stuff appear a bit outdated today since this was written way back in the 80s. Otherwise this is a good book to read.<br /><br />After reading Congo I will see monkeys and apes with a lot more respect. The gorilla is described to be far more docile creature than the chimpanzees, however fearsome they appear. Don't judge a book by the cover (pun intended). I was actually surprised by such tidbits in the book regarding primate behaviour. Enjoy the adventure !</span>
  <a data-text-id="14376399476737614648" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/7653473-congo">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49365462-w?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2038975986" class="readable"

  <span id="freeText10854556832542273061" style="display:none">Michael Crichton called this book a continuation of the tradition of H.Rider Haggard's King Solomon's Mines. The book didn't impress me all that much.<br /><br />A field expedition dies mysteriously in minutes,in the darkest region of Congo.In San Francisco,an extraordinary gorilla,named Amy,with a 620 sign vocabulary,may hold the secret to that carnage.Thankfully,however,the gorilla does not speak English.<br /><br />Another expedition,is sent to investigate.After that comes the lost city of Zinj,fights with gorillas and an exploding volcano.These are the type of ingredients loved by Hollywood.<br /><br />The book was yet another commercial success for Crichton,and also became a major motion picture.I haven't seen it,nor do I intend to.Still remember how bored I was watching Jurassic Park,another film of a Crichton book.<br /><br />Yet another one of his books,which I struggled to finish,and which at times literally put me to sleep.<br /><br />1.5 stars,rounded up</span>

<div id="review_2854509000" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2854509000" />
    <a title="Dennis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/64621419-dennis"><img alt="Dennis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604273386p2/64621419.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2854509000?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dennis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dennis" href="/user/show/64621419-dennis">Dennis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/10419175-congo">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64621419-dennis?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64621419-dennis?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2854509000" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7236340207796879200">German review <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1902846256' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a>.<br/><br/>A little over two decades ago this was my introduction to Michael Crichton. It‘s also the first novel that someone had ever gifted to me, if I remember correctly.<br/><br/>So, thank you aunt Ilona. I became a fan of the author immediately.<br/><br/>Reading this again in 2019, this time in it’s original language, it was once more a lot of fun. Even though much of it is very dated and in fact was already dated when I first read this back in 1995.<br/><br/>In 1979 a Congo expedition gets attacked and killed i</span>
  <span id="freeText7236340207796879200" style="display:none">German review <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1902846256" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.<br /><br />A little over two decades ago this was my introduction to Michael Crichton. It‘s also the first novel that someone had ever gifted to me, if I remember correctly.<br /><br />So, thank you aunt Ilona. I became a fan of the author immediately.<br /><br />Reading this again in 2019, this time in it’s original language, it was once more a lot of fun. Even though much of it is very dated and in fact was already dated when I first read this back in 1995.<br /><br />In 1979 a Congo expedition gets attacked and killed in a matter of minutes. The video transmission from the geologists‘ camp that their sponsor studies back in Houston is disturbing. The camp is completely destroyed, there are dead bodies everywhere, their skulls crushed, and for a short moment there’s something moving in front of the camera. And it is not human.<br /><br />A second expedition is hastily prepared, because the company is in a race with a Japanese/German consortium to find the Lost City of Zinj, which they believe is buried somewhere in the dense tropical rainforest of the Congo. They are looking for a scarce type of diamond that’s of tremendous value as a semiconductor and is expected to push computing to another level. Billions of dollars are at stake.<br /><br />Primatologist Peter Elliot who works with Amy, a Gorilla that has learned sign language and has a vocabulary of 620 signs, is planning to go to the Congo as well. Recently Amy has told him of nightmares that she’s having and a couple of pictures that she‘s painted resemble a Portugeses print that is showing the Lost City of Zinj. But how can that be? The print is from 1642 and they’re not even sure the city it shows does really exist. Enter the aforementioned Congo expedition and the fact that the company is contacting Elliot for spoilery reasons, and off to the Congo they are. Taking Amy with them and trying to find the lost city, albeit for very different reasons.<br /><br />The main story is still an exciting thriller in an exotic setting, as the group of people is facing lots of different obstacles, from warlords and cannibals to wild animals, thunderstorms, volcanoes, raging rivers and the generally unforgiving nature of the rainforest.<br /><br />The technical parts of the book though, even though they are incorporated reasonably well, take up too much room. Epecially from today’s perspective, as they have not aged very well. Which is to be expected, since the book is almost 40 years old by now and the computer industry has advanced so much that what was once intended to be science-fiction is now almost kinda cute in how backward it all is.<br /><br />If you are able to look past this fact, there are still enough interesting things to learn from the several infodumps. Especially the parts concerned with the early exploration of the African continent and the ones about animal research I found quite interesting. And from a historical standpoint the computing part might be interesting for some as well, even though it wasn’t for me.<br /><br />What makes this a four star read still, for me personally, is the great setting, the thrilling adventure and the lovable Amy. The adorable mountain gorilla is by far the best character in this book and I completely fell in love with her and would adopt her without hesitation.<br /><br />I can still see why this book made me a fan of Michael Crichton all those years ago.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7236340207796879200" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_136577076" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/136577076" />
    <a title="Ryan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1500718-ryan"><img alt="Ryan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1238846167p2/1500718.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/136577076?book_show_action=true">Dec 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ryan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ryan" href="/user/show/1500718-ryan">Ryan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer136577076" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10497086885136416884">Michael Crichton's work should be considered the epitome of geek literature (AKA science fiction, genre fiction, or speculative fiction), but was somehow embraced by the mainstream -- so much so that even if the academic crowd doesn't take him very seriously, Crichton still addressed Congress. Genre fiction is such a dismissive term, so Crichton was given his own genre: it's not geek; it's a "techno thriller."<br/><br/><i>Congo</i>, published in 1980, has all of Crichton's geekiest motifs, including a heroine wh</span>
  <span id="freeText10497086885136416884" style="display:none">Michael Crichton's work should be considered the epitome of geek literature (AKA science fiction, genre fiction, or speculative fiction), but was somehow embraced by the mainstream -- so much so that even if the academic crowd doesn't take him very seriously, Crichton still addressed Congress. Genre fiction is such a dismissive term, so Crichton was given his own genre: it's not geek; it's a "techno thriller."<br /><br /><i>Congo</i>, published in 1980, has all of Crichton's geekiest motifs, including a heroine whose tragic flaw is revealed on -- get this -- a computer printout. It's a pretty obvious way of characterizing one's hero, but it works. And give him credit, unlike in <i>The Andromeda Strain</i>, Crichton actually has characters with personalities and internal conflicts in <i>Congo</i>. Clearly, this is an author on the rise.<br /><br /><i>Congo</i> works in the same way that <i>Sphere</i> (1987) and <i>Jurassic Park</i> (1990) -- my favorite Crichton titles -- work. A team of scientists is sent on a dangerous mission that will require technical expertise, ingenuity, and a conflict between ambition and responsibility. I love that Crichton takes the ideal neutrality and benefits of science and juxtaposes them with the realities of funding, application, and career ambition. These three works also serve to map out what I believe is Crichton approaching and reaching the peak of his writing. My only wish is that I would have read <i>Congo</i> first, rather than third.<br /><br /><i>Congo</i> was not only published first in this thematic and structural trilogy, but it is clear that Crichton was consciously improving his writing in each of these novels. In <i>Congo</i>, he establishes the pattern by opening with a cool setting and a cool premise: jungle ruins and highly trained attack gorillas. Not bad.<br /><br />But he can do better.<br /><br /><i>Sphere</i> features the ocean floor and an alien technology that tests humanity's character. The characters are also more complex and engaging in <i>Sphere</i>, and I especially enjoyed Crichton's decision to make psychologist Norman Johnson the hero. <i>Sphere</i> is great, so everyone must have quite naturally expected that Crichton would begin the 1990s with his authorial decline.<br /><br />But then:<br /><br />In <i>Jurassic Park</i>, dinosaurs are brought back to life through cloning technology on a privately owned tropical island. Unbelievable! And let's not forget about Alan Grant and Ian Malcolm, arguably Crichton's most memorable academics, battling dinosaurs (don't gorillas just seem so "small potatoes" in comparison?) with nothing but their wits.<br /><br />So, for me, <i>Congo</i> is a very good work, but not a great one. However, perhaps this is only if we measure Crichton against himself.<br /><br />And it does not change the fact that <i>Congo</i>, <i>Sphere</i>, and <i>Jurassic Park</i> should be considered a required "trilogy" for all geeks -- sorry -- I meant "required reading for all 'techno thriller enthusiasts.'"</span>
  <a data-text-id="10497086885136416884" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Vimal Thiagarajan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27250071-vimal-thiagarajan"><img alt="Vimal Thiagarajan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1511490522p2/27250071.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1721019191?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vimal Thiagarajan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vimal Thiagarajan" href="/user/show/27250071-vimal-thiagarajan">Vimal Thiagarajan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1721019191" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6438996035844492198">A seriously good techno-thriller which had me wondering for the most part. Of course, it being written in the eighties not all of the technology that Crichton uses to construct the story are still relevant, but their canny placement in the narrative to resolve tangles or deliver surprise twists was simply too neat. The characters where typical thriller material - not sufficiently developed, but not boring either. Amy the talking Gorilla simply stood out, and I learned a good deal about the tropi</span>
  <span id="freeText6438996035844492198" style="display:none">A seriously good techno-thriller which had me wondering for the most part. Of course, it being written in the eighties not all of the technology that Crichton uses to construct the story are still relevant, but their canny placement in the narrative to resolve tangles or deliver surprise twists was simply too neat. The characters where typical thriller material - not sufficiently developed, but not boring either. Amy the talking Gorilla simply stood out, and I learned a good deal about the tropical rain forests of the Congo.<br /><br />My only gripes with the book were to do with a few logical loopholes - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the logistics devised for landing the second team in Congo without anyone noticing wasn't convincing, Elliot's reason to take Amy to the Congo wasn't sound enough, the Gorilla trance during the final attack on listening to the recording was simply laughable  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />The 5-page reference section at the end of the book linking his hundreds of references to particular paragraphs in the book simply flattened me. A bonus stunner came when I read in the internet that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[in 2004, scientists discovered a new freakin ape species in the Congo for real as Crichton had postulated!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> If this is one of his least popular thrillers, I just can't wait to pick up his other ones.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6438996035844492198" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Karl Marberger" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58621278-karl-marberger"><img alt="Karl Marberger" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593713350p2/58621278.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1976401621?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karl Marberger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karl Marberger" href="/user/show/58621278-karl-marberger">Karl Marberger</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/10419175-congo">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58621278-karl-marberger?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1976401621" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12288071409944901159">Crichton loved to go into intricate, technical detail with all of the little scientific specifics in his writing. Often they’re informative and interesting. But in a novel, this only lasts so long before it actually gets a wee bit repetitive and even annoying. <br/><br/>One example in this book; at one point, you’ll spend 3 pages reading about the biology, habitat, and behavior of hippos in order to build up to a 1/2 page confrontation with a bull hippo. <br/><br/>Often, Crichton spends to much time on these lectur</span>
  <span id="freeText12288071409944901159" style="display:none">Crichton loved to go into intricate, technical detail with all of the little scientific specifics in his writing. Often they’re informative and interesting. But in a novel, this only lasts so long before it actually gets a wee bit repetitive and even annoying. <br /><br />One example in this book; at one point, you’ll spend 3 pages reading about the biology, habitat, and behavior of hippos in order to build up to a 1/2 page confrontation with a bull hippo. <br /><br />Often, Crichton spends to much time on these lectures and not enough on his plot and characters. In this book, you learn a lot about gorillas, animal husbandry, African ecosystems and electrical engineering, but this is all at the expense of plot build, character development, and good dialogue; of which there is none. Completely lacking in all of the elements of a fun read.<br /><br />It did not hold my interest very well at all. For a 316 page book, it took me way to long to read. Don’t get me wrong, I’m all for learning something when reading a book, but I need to be captivated first.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12288071409944901159" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2838753" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9333268791996910357">I saw this on Chris' list and it triggered an old, funny memory. Now, I did read this book -- back in high school I went through a Michael Crichton phase and his books being as they are, I managed to read through his -- dare I say oevure? -- in a summer (don't recall which summer, tho')<br/><br/>The odd memory that Chris triggered however, has to to do with the movie Congo. I had a good friend in high school, wonderful fella, still a great friend. About the time we were seniors, he started dating -- or as</span>
  <span id="freeText9333268791996910357" style="display:none">I saw this on Chris' list and it triggered an old, funny memory. Now, I did read this book -- back in high school I went through a Michael Crichton phase and his books being as they are, I managed to read through his -- dare I say oevure? -- in a summer (don't recall which summer, tho')<br /><br />The odd memory that Chris triggered however, has to to do with the movie Congo. I had a good friend in high school, wonderful fella, still a great friend. About the time we were seniors, he started dating -- or as the kids say, "going steady" with a...I think she was a sophomore at the time. The point is, Saturday nights I'd ask him:<br /><br />"What are you doing tonight?"<br />"We rented Congo."<br />"You rented that last week."<br />"..."<br /><br />And -- not lying -- we had the exchange roughly twice a month for the life of their relationship (about the length of the school year). Thus, when anyone in our circle of friends got lucky (for most of us a rare occurrence), we referred to it as "watching Congo." To use it in a sentence...<br /><br />"You watch Congo on Saturday?"<br />"You know how I roll."<br /><br />Etc., et.al.<br /><br />(granted, at the time, no one I knew said "how I roll," but it sounds better)<br /><br />In regards to the actual book, the only thing I remember is that I did not care much for it.<br /><br />~cpd<br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12102458040076219155">Not bad in places...other times it's sort of a "puleez" book. Again Crichton has one that could have been better. The best I suppose I can say is..it wasn't as lame as the movie. So full of PC political rhetoric it seemed to me that any story got lost.<br/><br/><br/><br/><br/>************ Spoilers below Line ***********<br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[The "Amy" character is just too sweet for words...I had to take insulin. I love animals, really I do, not setting up a joke here about eating meat. (Though I do eat meat). But I love animal</span></span>
  <span id="freeText12102458040076219155" style="display:none">Not bad in places...other times it's sort of a "puleez" book. Again Crichton has one that could have been better. The best I suppose I can say is..it wasn't as lame as the movie. So full of PC political rhetoric it seemed to me that any story got lost.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br />************ Spoilers below Line ***********<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The "Amy" character is just too sweet for words...I had to take insulin. I love animals, really I do, not setting up a joke here about eating meat. (Though I do eat meat). But I love animals and I know that Gorillas are not actually predators (Chimpanzees are,but that's another discussion)... BUT, the sign language using Gorilla and of course the secret of the "bad things" as Amy calls the aggressive gorillas (that they were made evil by evil humans) and the whole technology and advancement and the companies who build it are ALWAYS EVIL theme was for me just to much of a head slapper. Personally I enjoy having a flush toilet, using my computer, living in a dwelling that has heat in the winter and cooling in the summer, watching TV, listening to music whenever I like, having light at my fingertips when I want to read a book at night and all the other evil advances that have gotten us out of the jungle expanded our life spans to more than 30 or 40 years and so on. AND I believe it's possible to have those things without destroying nature and don't think all technological groups are out to destroy nature.<br /><br />The book is in other words at times silly...though not as silly as the movie with Amy's "talking backpack"... Oh come on please. <br /><br />I wonder if by now there's an entire tribe of Gorillas who "speak" sign language. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> </span>

<div id="review_530033337" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/530033337" />
    <a title="Corey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12949855-corey"><img alt="Corey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604267805p2/12949855.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/530033337?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Corey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Corey" href="/user/show/12949855-corey">Corey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780061782558" href="/book/show/6326950-congo">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12949855-corey?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12949855-corey?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer530033337" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6501979503472535020">Another intriguing tale by the late Michael Crichton, and Congo was way ahead of it's time. <br/><br/>After an expedition of geologists are brutally killed deep in the rainforest of the Congo, the replacement team, led by the Project Supervisor Karen Ross, along with primatologist Peter Elliott and his female gorilla Amy, who is able to communicate with humans through the use of sign language. Unknown with what they are up against, accept for the video transmission of the aftermath, a camp destroyed, equi</span>
  <span id="freeText6501979503472535020" style="display:none">Another intriguing tale by the late Michael Crichton, and Congo was way ahead of it's time. <br /><br />After an expedition of geologists are brutally killed deep in the rainforest of the Congo, the replacement team, led by the Project Supervisor Karen Ross, along with primatologist Peter Elliott and his female gorilla Amy, who is able to communicate with humans through the use of sign language. Unknown with what they are up against, accept for the video transmission of the aftermath, a camp destroyed, equipment shattered along with dead bodies, Amy has a hobby in finger painting, and her latest drawing has left Peter disturbed with what it represents, a print dating back to the 1600's, a drawing of an ancient lost city. The expedition heads into the Congo searching for deposits of valuable diamonds for an unknown project, where they find a lost world and more than they bargained for.<br /><br />Started out really slow, didn't know where things were heading, but then once the group arrives in the Congo, I couldn't put it down! Some may argue that this was Crichton's worst ever novel, I've read many reviews saying it was cheesy and far-fetched, which I can relate to, but I still found it to just be a fun roller-coaster of science fiction and adventure, and with my love and passion for gorillas, watching King Kong and Mighty Joe Young as a child, I realized this book was for me!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6501979503472535020" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1769529966" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1769529966" />
    <a title="Sud666" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36890366-sud666"><img alt="Sud666" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1418437112p2/36890366.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1769529966?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sud666" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sud666" href="/user/show/36890366-sud666">Sud666</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36890366-sud666?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1769529966" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15633564031957747850">Congo was written in 1980 by Michael Crichton. With a few, very minor details (such as gushing over how awesome it is to have a comuter with 256K memory) this is a tale that reads very well to this day.<br/><br/>In 1979, due to the increasing demands of the computer industry there were a large number of companies that were seeking to find industrial grade diamonds, as opposed to the jewelry type of diamonds. Specifically they were looking for Type IIb boron-coated blue diamonds used to build a variety of </span>
  <span id="freeText15633564031957747850" style="display:none">Congo was written in 1980 by Michael Crichton. With a few, very minor details (such as gushing over how awesome it is to have a comuter with 256K memory) this is a tale that reads very well to this day.<br /><br />In 1979, due to the increasing demands of the computer industry there were a large number of companies that were seeking to find industrial grade diamonds, as opposed to the jewelry type of diamonds. Specifically they were looking for Type IIb boron-coated blue diamonds used to build a variety of chips and circuit boards. Unfortunately, the place to find these diamonds is in the Congo. Specifically in the drainage basin of the Congo River, close to Zaire.<br /><br />The company in the story (ERTS) sends in a site team that records some success in possibly finding a good mining source for these diamonds. This could potentially be worth billions. But, the last transmission from the team was very strange. It showed a destroyed camp and a grainy, unfocused image of what seemed like either a man or a primate of some sort. But no one is sure what it is exactly, until someone clears up the image and finds what looks like a gray furred gorilla. The problem is no gorilla has ever exhibited the behavior of the one in the image and there are no gray furred gorillas. So the second ERTS field team is put in touch with Dr. Elliott of U.C. Berkeley, a leading Primatologist. Dr. Elliot works with a juvenile female gorilla named Amy. Amy is able to communicate through Sign Language. Dr. Elliott, Amy and Dr. Ross (the ERTS lead) travel to Africa to first recruit their guide- a skilled guide/mercenary known as Capt. Munro.<br />As the story develops, we go through a variety of trouble from competing firms, civil wars, rebels, cannibals and hostile tribes. Yet, as the story develops we find that there might be something to these rumors of "something" in the deep jungle. It seems that a long time ago there was a fabled lost city-Zinj. Yet something or someone killed the last 8 man team sent in. Now the ERTS team must use Amy and Dr. Elliott's expertise to try to figure out what was on that video tape and what killed the last team. I will not spoil the story for you and this is one that is worth reading yourself to find out what is going on.<br /><br />As usual, Crichton is able to seamlessly blend in science and action and great characters to create a wonderfully engrossing story. Full of fascinating information such as a a historical background of exploration in the Congo region, to the variety of primates and tribes that abound in the region, as well as fascinating details about how Primate Research, especially focusing on gorillas, works. I had no idea about some of the ways in which Primatologists interpreted and communicated with gorillas. The story is fast paced and the characters of Capt Munro, Amy and Dr. Elliott steal the show.<br /><br />While this isn't quite the novel that Jurassic Park or Lost World was, this is still a great read. Crichton is engaging and as always-he knows his stuff. From biology and ecology to primatology and geology. This is science presented in easy to understand terms, but is no less fascinating for that reason. If you are looking for a book that's 1 part action adventure, 1 part science information and 1 part murder mystery-then this is for you. Of course, if you are a Crichton fan you will enjoy this one quite a bit. Just ignore the computer terms used-this is from 1980 and it is safe to say that numbers like 128k and 256K do not engender gasps of astonishment anymore. If they do, it is for the opposite reason than what was expressed in 1980.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15633564031957747850" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2097945113" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2097945113" />
    <a title="Baz MW" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12910835-baz-mw"><img alt="Baz MW" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570576009p2/12910835.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2097945113?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Baz MW" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Baz MW" href="/user/show/12910835-baz-mw">Baz MW</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2097945113" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9681642142940420677">Congo is very well researched (which is clear from the bibliography alone). And while some of the information is outdated now (forty years after the book was written), it was certainly ahead of its time.<br/><br/>That being said, this might just be the last Michael Crichton book that I read. While his writing has certainly improved since reading The Terminal Man (published 1971), his archaic personality that he inputs into his narration unfortunately has not (though I held out hope).<br/><br/>His (obviously persona</span>
  <span id="freeText9681642142940420677" style="display:none">Congo is very well researched (which is clear from the bibliography alone). And while some of the information is outdated now (forty years after the book was written), it was certainly ahead of its time.<br /><br />That being said, this might just be the last Michael Crichton book that I read. While his writing has certainly improved since reading The Terminal Man (published 1971), his archaic personality that he inputs into his narration unfortunately has not (though I held out hope).<br /><br />His (obviously personal) negative opinions of women and other races are peppered throughout the narrated dialogue and this is hard to get past... even for me, a white man.<br /><br />While we should judge an artist for their art alone, in this instance, the distraction of Crichton’s obvious misogyny and racial ignorance affects the reading of this and so affects my rating. I love the premise of this book. The delivery fell short.<br /><br />Some great action and fantastic characters are reeled in by chapters that leave the reader feeling short-changed by scenes that are under kneaded. <br /><br />3 to 3.5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9681642142940420677" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2303058464" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2303058464" />
    <a title="Michael Chrobak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33791289-michael-chrobak"><img alt="Michael Chrobak" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479237284p2/33791289.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2303058464?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Chrobak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Chrobak" href="/user/show/33791289-michael-chrobak">Michael Chrobak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780613100557" href="/book/show/232185.Congo">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2303058464" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1703905574938908692">Going into this book, I’ll admit I was really excited. I had heard so many good things about Crichton, and though I don't recall reading any of his books, I’ve most likely watched all of the movies based on his books. For the most part, I loved it!<br/><br/>Crichton is such an fantastic storyteller. The pace of the book is near perfect, and the progression of events throughout the first 90% of the book kept me more than intrigued. In fact, this was easily one of my fastest reads and could have been comple</span>
  <span id="freeText1703905574938908692" style="display:none">Going into this book, I’ll admit I was really excited. I had heard so many good things about Crichton, and though I don't recall reading any of his books, I’ve most likely watched all of the movies based on his books. For the most part, I loved it!<br /><br />Crichton is such an fantastic storyteller. The pace of the book is near perfect, and the progression of events throughout the first 90% of the book kept me more than intrigued. In fact, this was easily one of my fastest reads and could have been completed even faster if I hadn’t had so many other distractions.<br /><br />​The characters were believable and well crafted, the overlapping goals of the three main characters were well designed, and the addition of a talking (okay, signing) gorilla was definitely a treat.<br /><br />Though I have to say I found the story to be a bit hodgepodge, with fairly diverse elements converging together, it was all relative to the story, for the most part. There are some items that I didn’t feel needed to be included; and there are some amazing technologies that truly didn’t seem to fit with the era this book was supposedly based in. Like a software program that takes about a day to learn how to translate the language of a group of apes using only a few small sample verbal recordings, and yet Crichton imagined these apes to speak concurrently with both voices (grunts and huffs) and hand gestures. Though only the vocals were analyzed, the software program was still able to translate enough of the language to let the scientists communicate with the apes.<br /><br />The basic story is this: a mining corporation is in pursuit of a type of diamond that has little value from the perspective of fashion, due to the tainted blue coloring, but has enormous value for computer hardware applications. Their exploration team, deep in the Congo, suddenly stops reporting, and when the home office obtains control of the video equipment and is able to use it to view the campsite where the team was stationed, they find a grim scene.<br /><br />One of their most talented scientists decides she is going to take it on herself to lead the next team, even though she has zero field experience. (Okay, I'll suspend disbelief and just run with it.) However, it seems the company is far more interested in finding the diamonds and doesn't care about recovering the bodies or equipment from the last team. Based on a few seconds of video footage they were able to capture from the event that killed their previous team, Ross decides she wants to take a primate expert with her, and contacts a scientist who is experimenting with teaching communication skills to a young female ape named Amy, who becomes an important figure in the story, and even has a good portion of dialogue throughout. As per any good thriller, there are setbacks around every corner, and the team is forced to navigate around those while all the time racing against an international conglomerate set on beating them to the discovery of the diamonds.<br /><br />​I did find the setbacks and conflicts to be handled far too easily. For example, in one part, the aircraft the team is using is suddenly under fire from radar controlled anti-aircraft missiles being launched from the ground, and they're just like, "Let's open the back cargo door and throw out some chaff." Problem solved. <br /><br />As mentioned earlier, the overall quality of the writing and the story are well crafted, however, there are several points during which Crichton takes the reader on a lengthy and mostly unnecessary sidebar. For example, though the action and intrigue in one section is becoming fairly intense, we suddenly spend 4 or 5 pages getting a history lesson on one of the technologies used in the book. This happens several times throughout the novel, so it appears to be intentionally written this way. I found those parts to be long-winded, distracting, and fairly dull.<br /><br />The end of the book also appears to have been written specifically with the hope that the book would become either a movie or perhaps a video game. There are so many final conflicts that merge together at the exact time, it’s almost impossible to believe the heroes will ever survive. And then, suddenly, it’s over. The team does exactly what they need to do to get out of every conflict that cropped up in the final chapter and we are left with a fairly small epilogue to wrap everything up, which it really doesn’t do.<br />​<br />Overall I’m giving this one 3.5 stars, and I’m crossing my fingers that the next Crichton novel I read is better.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1703905574938908692" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17662698360952475130" style="display:none">what could have been a great adventure book turned out to be a barely mediocre writing effort on behalf of Crichton.         <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer20228256&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer20228256" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11236846103935113877">Michael Crichton books all start off with this huge technological hook and are excellent at grabbing you by your ear and dragging you along, but somewhere along the way he fizzles. It's like he has this great idea, but can't figure out a way for his protagonists to create a successful ending. Andromeda Strain, the virus floats off into space--woo hoo. Sphere--the whole adventure was imaginary, woo hoo. Congo, earthquake wipes out all the lovely evidence and negates the whole adventure...boo hoo.</span>
  <span id="freeText11236846103935113877" style="display:none">Michael Crichton books all start off with this huge technological hook and are excellent at grabbing you by your ear and dragging you along, but somewhere along the way he fizzles. It's like he has this great idea, but can't figure out a way for his protagonists to create a successful ending. Andromeda Strain, the virus floats off into space--woo hoo. Sphere--the whole adventure was imaginary, woo hoo. Congo, earthquake wipes out all the lovely evidence and negates the whole adventure...boo hoo. Ocassionally MC will get it right, but even with Juraissic Park, where the characters manage to escape with their lives--the ending is still ambivalent. Nothing was truly resolved. Quit being so wishy-washy MC and give us an ending we can sink our teeth into! </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2029610014" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2029610014" />
    <a title="Josh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/221650-josh"><img alt="Josh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453197716p2/221650.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2029610014?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Josh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Josh" href="/user/show/221650-josh">Josh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/221650-josh?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2029610014" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8972073595958370737">I was at Costco the other day and saw the cover art for a book that looked a lot like Jurassic Park, then did a double take when I saw Michael Crichton’s name on it. Apparently Mr. Crichton is the Tupac of fiction, now with his 3rd book released since his death. I was nearly intrigued enough to buy the book and then thought to myself, “how many of his books have been out for decades that I haven’t even read yet?” Remembering I had Congo sitting on my shelf for years, I decided to finally read it</span>
  <span id="freeText8972073595958370737" style="display:none">I was at Costco the other day and saw the cover art for a book that looked a lot like Jurassic Park, then did a double take when I saw Michael Crichton’s name on it. Apparently Mr. Crichton is the Tupac of fiction, now with his 3rd book released since his death. I was nearly intrigued enough to buy the book and then thought to myself, “how many of his books have been out for decades that I haven’t even read yet?” Remembering I had Congo sitting on my shelf for years, I decided to finally read it, forgoing my reluctance based on the terrible movie. I can say that the book is definitely better than the movie, but still a far cry from Crichton’s best.<br /> <br />One thing that Crichton has never excelled at is in-depth characters and Congo does nothing to make an exception of that. Of all the primary characters in the novel, the one with the most depth isn’t even human. Amy, the hyper-intelligent gorilla who joins the expedition into the Congo, is the only character that really shows growth and something resembling a full character arc. Of the other characters, Karen Ross is the callous geologist who shows no empathy for her colleagues and whose mind is only on money and the mission of finding diamonds in the lost city of Zinj. There’s Peter Elliot, the intelligent yet naive primatologist, who instantly agreed to go on an incredibly dangerous mission simply because he was wanting to take Amy into the jungle anyway. And Munro, who admittedly is much more fun to read about than the previous two, is the confident guide who is there because he’s the best at what he does. For such a hardened, tough character, Munro is the definitely the most empathetic and the only one besides Peter who treats Amy as more than just an animal. He’s also just an all around bad-ass.<br /> <br />The story gets going immediately as an expedition into the Congo is wiped out by mysterious assailants on the hunt for diamonds. So naturally a second expedition is put together immediately. Time is of the essence, as the Americans race against the Euro-Japanese Consortium, a rival competitor on the search for the same diamonds and the same lost city of Zinj. The quick pace of the novel is frequently interrupted by info dumps regarding technology and how quickly it’s advancing. These interludes might have been more interesting if the technology in question wasn’t nearly 40 years old now (at one point they talk about a massive worldwide network of computers being an unlikely possibility for the future.) Although I suppose comparing the technology of that time, and the characters being so excited about achieving things which are so trivial today, is interesting enough in its own right. To me, this emphasis on technology sort of detracts from the mystery of hunting down a mythical city and lost civilization in the middle of the world’s largest jungle. Maybe that’s what Crichton was going for: What if Dr Livingston had had satellite tracking and laser-guided machine guns on his adventures in Africa? <br /> <br />All in all, it’s a fun book with Crichton’s trademark addicting “must turn another page” style. While it starts with great promise, it ended leaving me a tad underwhelmed. It’s not that the book didn’t fulfill the promises laid out in the beginning, it’s just that once the veil was lifted, the mystery outweighed the reality. The strange and mysterious inhabitants of the city weren’t so strange once we see them, just angry (okay, we all know they’re grey gorillas. We all saw the dumb movie.) And as for the city, the characters even comment on how unremarkable it is. This city and its inhabitants were all fictional, so if they are mundane, it’s only because the author made them so. While the book had a reasonably satisfying ending, I couldn’t help but wonder, “ultimately, what was the point?” The characters, other than the gorilla, didn’t really grow or seem to overcome their flaws for the experience. Also, the frequent passages of “later, they will recount that...” clearly tell us that the characters survive the experience, which just further saps the tension the drama. It’s a fun book, and I don’t regret reading it, but it doesn’t hold a candle to Sphere or Jurassic Park.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8972073595958370737" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText18191557964168847541" style="display:none">'The more experience and insight I obtain into human nature, the more convinced do o become that the greater portion of a man is purely animal'-Henry Morton Stanley,1887.<br />INTRO.<br />Only prejudice, and a trick of the Mercator's projection, prevents us from recognizing the enormity of the African continent.Covering nearly twelve million square miles,Africa is almost as large as North America and Europe combined. Congo enlightened me on mineral deposits and its mining.<br />If you have not read this book then you need to.</span>

<div id="review_871648906" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/871648906" />
    <a title="Benjamin Stahl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16968146-benjamin-stahl"><img alt="Benjamin Stahl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592923113p2/16968146.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
