        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer871648906" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8260083664192385985"><b>A <i>Heartbreak Hipster</i> Review</b><br/><br/><i>Congo</i> is definitely the most disappointing Crichton book I have read so far. <br/><br/>I expected this to be silly but also fun. I haven't seen the movie and I can't say I'm in any hurry to do so. The only thing I did know about this book was that it involved a talking gorilla, a bunch of scientists and an unknown species of hostile apes. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394832455i/8913358.jpg' width='200' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394832455i/8913359.jpg' width='200' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Fucking horrible creatures. But gorillas are okay.</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394832455i/8913360._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394832455i/8913361._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>According to Dr Naan - one who is seemingly incapable of giving a straight fucking answer wh</span>
  <span id="freeText8260083664192385985" style="display:none"><b>A <i>Heartbreak Hipster</i> Review</b><br><br><i>Congo</i> is definitely the most disappointing Crichton book I have read so far. <br><br>I expected this to be silly but also fun. I haven't seen the movie and I can't say I'm in any hurry to do so. The only thing I did know about this book was that it involved a talking gorilla, a bunch of scientists and an unknown species of hostile apes. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394832455i/8913358.jpg" width="200" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394832455i/8913359.jpg" width="200" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Fucking horrible creatures. But gorillas are okay.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394832455i/8913360._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394832455i/8913361._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>According to Dr Naan - one who is seemingly incapable of giving a straight fucking answer when he’s about his UK visa, yet can articulate like Shakespeare when it comes to his controversial theories that 80% of females aged 15-40 are expected to have at least one sexual dream in which they get raped by three gorillas simultaneously. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394837428i/8914229.jpg" width="250" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394837428i/8914230.png" width="150" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>I mean, maybe it’s true. But it still doesn’t justify what he and his cousins did to that poor little girl ...</b> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394837428i/8914231._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Also, according to my ex-girlfriend's brother, some girls fantasise their exes getting their ass neatly handed to them by a steroid-fed mountain gorilla.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394837428i/8914232._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So that's my review of <i>Luke Neely</i>. He may have screwed a lot of things up, but deep down I do believe he has a heart of gold and all it takes is ... <br><br><b>Oh ... Wait.<br><br>I'm supposed to be reviewing <i>Congo</i> aren't I?</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394837428i/8914234._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Well, Michael Crichton's <i>Congo</i> not only promises but delivers a genuinely intriguing premise. After an American expedition, seek-<br>ing diamonds in the Congo, gets savaged under strange circumstances, a rescue mission is sent in. These idiots enter the country under the political radar because civil war is breaking out and indigenous tribes are attacking and killing innocent civilians. <br>Karen Ross commands the ERTS Rescue Expedition. She enlists the help of an ex-mercenary named Munro. And then our true protagonists - Dr Elliot and his <i>Ameslan</i>-trained gorilla, Amy - join from San Francisco, thinking to escape the smell of fecal matter.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394837428i/8914235.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Now listen here people, because Mikey's not finished yet. Little does Elliot know that his cold-natured scientist friend has another agenda: she wants to locate and excavate the diamond mines beneath some active volcano. <i>Oh, I thought we mentioned that on the brochure</i> ...<br><br>Anyway, this idea introduces various concepts. All of them should have been awesome in the hands of this talented author. There was me thinking outright gun-conflict between the Americans and Chinese (fighting for resources which belong to neither of them). Though it will probably sound lame, I had also wondered whether these strange combat-trained gorillas would eventually team with the Americans with Amy as their translator. And mostly I thought people were going to have their faces crushed by bloodthirsty gorillas - that is, when they weren't already being mauled by leopards or getting swallowed by giant snakes. An over the top jungle romp by Michael Crichton sounds like a perfect recipe.<br><br><b>But what do we get instead?</b> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395261683i/8973344.jpg" width="350" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>"<i>RECVD MESG AURL INFO PLS EXPLN.<br>AXIDENTL DISKVRY VRY XCITNG-DISCRIMNT</i>".<br><br><b>I'm sorry?</b><br><br>"<i>FUNXN COMPTRANLSS 99 CONFDNCE LIMITS TAPD.<br>AURL INFO (BRETHNG SOUNS) DEMNSTRTS</i>".<br><br><b>Oh, I see. Wait <i>what</i>?</b> <br><br>"<i>SOUND COMPLEX: ? AWAY - .5444 - .343.<br>SOUND COMPLEX: ? HERE - .6344 - .344</i>".<br><br><b>Okay, so what you're saying is -</b><br><br>"<i>Amy(2) = distncton (£ + w%R), means <br>Grilla x 12 (&lt;.435 + !!!) reslt = .004</i>".<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395263470i/8973490._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Michael, I can't understand <i>any</i> of this shit!!!!<br><br>What happened to the killer gorillas? <br><br>What happened to that ancient city?<br><br>What just happened to my <i>brain</i>?</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395263470i/8973491.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>If you had been my science teacher in high school then I probably <i>would've</i> had the guts to jump off the music-room balcony in front of my friends.</b> <br><br>Now of course I understand this is what fans expect from Mr. Crichton. But it does get a little over the top. And I can't imagine anyone actually taking the time to decipher what this guy is really saying. I am not asking him to dumb it down, <i>because unfortunately, that's no longer possible</i> ... <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395263470i/8973492._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>And I don't want him to write like a brainless idiot.</b> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395267154i/8973984.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>"Monkey make booboo on Man's face. "Ouchy!!!" Man scream. "I tink my nose is broked and my eye hang like yoyo". Man run round in circle. Monkey twist his head".</b><br><br>But I would have appreciated him putting just a <i>little</i> more thought into whether or not all his scientific expo was balanced with the thrills most fans also want. Even in his last novel, <i>Micro</i>, which was terribly written, I still gave it three stars because it had a good entertaining body count. Kudos to Michael for not just resorting to cheap mindless action scenes, but my <i>God</i>, was this a boring one to read!!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395313059i/8978434._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Does <i>this</i> look boring? Hell <i>no</i> it doesn't!!</b><br><br>But the book has barely anything exciting. I mean, he did introduce the <i>threat</i> of the cannibals earlier on. And he does go into the extensive causalities suffered by such other explorers that tried to navigate the Congo in their time. But the people in this story just breeze through the jungle as if it were their own backyard, fiddling with their high-tech gadgetry and setting up camp whenever they get tired. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380394209i/758982.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>There is some cutesy charm in having a communicative gorilla. And I am surprised to say the characters here were probably the most real I have seen by Crichton. But that is not to say they were <i>good</i>. Only that, for the first time ever, he has allowed his characters to show at least some human emotions in the face of imminent death. Ross actually <i>cries</i> when she realises the computer terminal in Houston won't save her from the Congo Army's missiles. While Munro feels mostly like a poor man's Quint (you know, that other caricature from <i>Jaws</i>) - I still liked the fact that he willingly stopped thinking about those silly diamonds and began acting like he genuinely cared about his life and the others. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395345467i/8982838.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Do you love <i>this</i> town, asshole?</b><br><br>So yeah, I'm not going to take the usual path with this writer and complain about his cardboard characters. These ones were more like <i>plastic</i>. If they were storage boxes, they'd look pretty boring but at least they’d get the job done. <br> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395359080i/8985468.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>This is a gongo. It rhymes with <i>Congo</i>.</b><br><br>Now, for God's sake, I told myself last time that I would cool it with these freaking reviews. I am putting more effort into <i>these</i> than I am with my actual writing. <i>Umm</i>. Okay. So while there was nothing really bad about this book, I can’t justify giving it any more than two stars. The writing was pretty good, standardly decent. And most of the characters were surprisingly not terrible. Only there was just so much more potential. Crichton did not so much <i>fail</i> to see that, as much as <i>know</i> it was there and simply not bother. That makes it harder to forgive.<br><i>Some</i> people died ... eventually. But their deaths were never actually <i>seen</i>. We're just told afterwards: some guy we didn't know the name of was found dead outside the campsite. It's kind of hard giving a shit about any of this. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395359080i/8985469.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Nobody important dies</i>!! <br><br>Even the few deaths that do occur just end up being so unsatisfying. I don't mean to sound like a Tarantino fan though. By "unsatisfying”, I only mean they didn't have any effect on the other characters whatsoever. Thus there was never any tension or threat established. The heroes just take note of each death and continue having overly technical conversations with each other. <br><br>(<i>Oh yeah - that just reminded me!! Crichton also took a leaf out of Stephen King's book: he kept reminding the reader that all the protagonists DO survive!! For some reason, he uses that device where the characters keep on commenting on everything that is happening - during some sort of interview after the events of the novel - just so you can rest assured your favourite characters are not going to die. Now this wouldn't have been so irritating had there actually been a purpose for it. But honestly, it serves nothing. There was no reason why we had to get the their retrospective thoughts as opposed to their present reactions</i>).<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395359080i/8985470._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>(ShUdDeRs In ReVuLsIoN ... )</b><br><br>The idea that they are trapped in the middle of the jungle, with a diminishing supply of ammunition, and the apes bound to attack them every night till they all get killed - that could and really should have worked. There was one part in particular - my favourite of the entire book - where they try to escape the jungle. While they do not <i>see</i> the gorillas during this, they eventually hear something coming from within the enveloping foliage. <i>An eerie orchestra of gentle sighing</i>; the sound the apes make when they are watching. Just hearing this is enough to creep the people out, driving them back to camp again. <br>That part was clever and effective because not only did it establish that they truly <i>were</i> trapped in their situation - it also attributed a subtle, though creepy, characteristic to the enemy. <br>Except there was <i>one</i> thing Mr. Medical Degree never stopped to think about. Once I thought about it, I felt like real hot shit and was crossing my fingers it would not occur to him. <br><br><b>Would you like to hear it?</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395359080i/8985471.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>So these guys are surrounded by dangerous jungle. Out of this jungle comes a marauding army of deadly gorillas. Bastards can attack them from every and any side. And to top that off, the ammunition and defence equipment's steadily running out. Too many sides to cover. Not enough supplies to keep it up. <br><br><b>Am I correct?</b> <br> <br>So all this worrying brings me to question the most obvious flaw in your set-up, Mr. Crichton. Like half a mile away there lies an empty city. Now forgive me if I've let my imagination get ahead of me, but surely these guys would be better off taking their shit into one small building, one small room, of that abandoned city. That way they only have one doorway to guard, as opposed to an encircling jungle. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395359080i/8985472.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>You go ahead and call me <i>pompous</i> ma'am. But I know who I’d rather take to the Congo.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395529495i/9010336._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Benjamin:</b> "The village should be just over that mountain". <br><br><b>Elliot:</b> "Thank God. I'm sick of this jungle".<br><br><b>Michael:</b> "Hey guys, have you seen these flowers?"<br><br><b>Benjamin:</b> "Yeah, Mike, they're nice. But now's not the - "<br><br><b>Michael:</b> "<i>Nice</i>. These not just <i>nice</i>".<br><br><b>Elliot:</b> Oh God, I think I just saw a gorilla behind that tree”.<br><br><b>Michael:</b> "I believe the correct term, Doctor, is <i>Beringei</i>".<br><br><b>Elliot:</b> "Is that their scientific name?"<br><br><b>Benjamin:</b> "Okay guys, who gives a shit? Where’s the gorilla? <i>Ahhhh GAAHD</i>!!!!"<br><br><b>Elliot:</b> "Oh Jesus!! The gorilla's got him!!"<br><br><b>Michael:</b> "Indeed ... umm. <i>Gosh</i>!!!"<br><br><b>Benjamin:</b> (Loses his arm. Screams incoherently).<br><br><b>Elliot:</b> "What should we do? Should we help him?<br><br><b>Michael:</b> "Ah now. You can't mess with nature"<br><br><b>Elliot:</b> "Yes but - "<br><br><b>Benjamin:</b> (Ribcage now crushed. Choking on his own blood).<br><br><b>Michael:</b> "Just watch how it kills. It's amazing".<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395522814i/9009843.png" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>I've always heard he was a prick in real life.</b><br><br>Anyway, so I can wrap this up and post it let me give my opinion of this book in a nutshell. <i>Congo</i> was overall a very disappointing book. Certainly not one I would recommend if you are reading Crichton for the first time. Some parts were kinda cool. But for all these, there were always two parts more that failed to hit the target one expects when reading something by this usually satisfying author. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8260083664192385985" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

			<a class="actionLink" href="/topic/show/21547239-buddy-read-congo-by-michael-crichton">Buddy Read: Congo by Michael Crichton </a>
		</td>
		<td class="nobreak">
		  28

	<tr>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xnCy/PjUK/Rf6nFzSEXZjzM1bbeI6lTMJ+VG5NVgULP8VtsuQ4rinPjBxRK/sNNQ5WqKf0Zn2qt8mwBVGCOiKQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TdLfEmUx3nNm8ccLWnjfJ4+0beUnzZRvuLyaZ5Ob8UF39LbA3m8XG8Hac2qtjdX4WeuKLelAGgjjwtzWXtgD2w==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/5194.Michael_Crichton">About Michael Crichton</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/5194.Michael_Crichton"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1359042651p3/5194.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/5194.Michael_Crichton">Michael Crichton
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
13,859
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12174267627152063247">Michael Crichton (1942-2008) was one of the most successful novelists of his generation, admired for his meticulous scientific research and fast-paced narrative. He graduated summa cum laude and earned his MD from Harvard Medical School in 1969. His first novel, <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18078737.Odds_On' title='Odds On' rel='nofollow noopener'>Odds On</a>
</i> (1966), was written under the pseudonym <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12619.John_Lange' title='John Lange' rel='nofollow noopener'>John Lange</a> and was followed by seven more Lange novels. He also wrote as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/85503.Michael_Douglas' title='Michael Douglas' rel='nofollow noopener'>Michael Doug</a></span>
  <span id="freeText12174267627152063247" style="display:none">Michael Crichton (1942-2008) was one of the most successful novelists of his generation, admired for his meticulous scientific research and fast-paced narrative. He graduated summa cum laude and earned his MD from Harvard Medical School in 1969. His first novel, <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18078737.Odds_On" title="Odds On" rel="nofollow noopener">Odds On</a>
</i> (1966), was written under the pseudonym <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12619.John_Lange" title="John Lange" rel="nofollow noopener">John Lange</a> and was followed by seven more Lange novels. He also wrote as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/85503.Michael_Douglas" title="Michael Douglas" rel="nofollow noopener">Michael Douglas</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/607284.Jeffery_Hudson" title="Jeffery Hudson" rel="nofollow noopener">Jeffery Hudson</a>. His novel <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7663.A_Case_of_Need" title="A Case of Need" rel="nofollow noopener">A Case of Need</a>
</i> won the Edgar Award in 1969. Popular throughout the world, he has sold more than 200 million books. His novels have been translated into thirty-eight languages, and thirteen have been made into films.<br /><br />Michael Crichton passed away from lymphoma in 2008. He was 66 years old.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12174267627152063247" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.

last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
React component will render its content.
-->
